<content>
1: package com.trulyfreeocr.pipeline;
2: 
3: import java.awt.image.BufferedImage;
4: 
5: import com.trulyfreeocr.model.SegmentedImage;
6: 
7: public class ImageSegmenter {
8: 
9:     private final int tileSize;
10:     private final double percentile;
11:     private final int inpaintRadius;
12: 
13:     public ImageSegmenter() {
14:         this(64, 0.95, 3);
15:     }
16: 
17:     public ImageSegmenter(int tileSize, double percentile, int inpaintRadius) {
18:         this.tileSize = tileSize;
19:         this.percentile = percentile;
20:         this.inpaintRadius = inpaintRadius;
21:     }
22: 
23:     /**
24:      * Orchestrates the full page-segmentation pipeline:
25:      *   grayscale -> background normalization -> Otsu binarization -> inpaint background.
26:      *
27:      * @param image  Input RGB page image (e.g. 300 DPI PDFBox render).
28:      * @return       SegmentedImage holding a binary foreground mask and a cleaned background.
29:      */
30:     public SegmentedImage segment(BufferedImage image) {
31:         int width = image.getWidth();
32:         int height = image.getHeight();
33: 
34:         // Step 1: Convert to grayscale
35:         int[] gray = toGrayscale(image);
36: 
37:         // Step 2: Background normalization
38:         double[] bgNormalized = backgroundNormalize(gray, width, height, tileSize);
39: 
40:         // Step 3: Otsu binarization
41:         int threshold = otsuThreshold(bgNormalized);
42:         BufferedImage foregroundMask = new BufferedImage(width, height, BufferedImage.TYPE_BYTE_BINARY);
43:         for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
44:             for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
45:                 int idx = y * width + x;
46:                 // Foreground = 0 (black), Background = 1 (white) in binary image
47:                 // Text is dark on light bg, so pixel <= threshold = foreground
48:                 if (gray[idx] <= threshold) {
49:                     foregroundMask.setRGB(x, y, 0xFF000000); // ARGB: black, full opacity
50:                 } else {
51:                     foregroundMask.setRGB(x, y, 0xFFFFFFFF); // ARGB: white, full opacity
52:                 }
53:             }
54:         }
55: 
56:         // Step 4: Cleaned background — fill text regions with surrounding color
57:         BufferedImage cleanedBackground = inpaintBackground(image, foregroundMask, inpaintRadius);
58: 
59:         return new SegmentedImage(foregroundMask, cleanedBackground);
60:     }
61: 
62:     /**
63:      * Converts an RGB BufferedImage to a flat int array of grayscale values
64:      * (0 = black, 255 = white) using the ITU-R BT.601 luma formula.
65:      *
66:      * Magic numbers in luma formula:
67:      *   0.299, 0.587, 0.114 — perception-weighted coefficients for R/G/B.
68:      *   Human vision is most sensitive to green, least to blue.
69:      *   These sum to 1.0, so neutral gray (R=G=B) maps to itself.
70:      *   This is the same formula used in JPEG, NTSC/PAL, and most image libraries.
71:      *
72:      * Bit shifts in RGB extraction:
73:      *   (rgb >> 16) & 0xFF  — extract the red  byte (bits 16-23 of 0xAARRGGBB)
74:      *   (rgb >>  8) & 0xFF  — extract the green byte (bits  8-15)
75:      *   rgb        & 0xFF  — extract the blue byte (bits  0-7)
76:      */
77:     private int[] toGrayscale(BufferedImage image) {
78:         int width = image.getWidth();
79:         int height = image.getHeight();
80:         int[] gray = new int[width * height];
81: 
82:         for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
83:             for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
84:                 int rgb = image.getRGB(x, y);
85:                 int r = (rgb >> 16) & 0xFF;
86:                 int g = (rgb >> 8) & 0xFF;
87:                 int b = rgb & 0xFF;
88:                 gray[y * width + x] = (int) (0.299 * r + 0.587 * g + 0.114 * b);
89:             }
90:         }
91:         return gray;
92:     }
93: 
94:     /**
95:      * Tile-based background normalization that corrects non-uniform illumination
96:      * (e.g. shadows, gradients, scanner vignetting).
97:      *
98:      * How it works:
99:      *   1. Divide the image into a grid of tiles (default 64x64 px).
100:      *   2. In each tile, estimate the "background level" as the 95th percentile
101:      *      of pixel intensities. Since text is dark on a light background, the
102:      *      bright tail of the histogram represents the page surface (background).
103:      *      The 95th percentile is used (instead of max) to be robust to noise.
104:      *   3. Build a smooth background surface across the page using bilinear
105:      *      interpolation between tile centers.
106:      *   4. Each pixel is then stretched: new_value = old_value * 255 / bg_estimate.
107:      *      Pixels at or near the background level map to 255 (white); dark text
108:      *      pixels stay dark because their value is far below the bg estimate.
109:      *
110:      * Magic numbers:
111:      *   tileSize = 64 — balances accuracy vs performance. 2^6 allows fast
112:      *     integer arithmetic for interpolation (tile centres are at multiples
113:      *     of 64).  Smaller = more detail but slower; larger = faster but coarser.
114:      *   0.95 — 95th percentile.  Picked empirically: the top 5% of brightness
115:      *     values in a tile are assumed to be background, not text or noise.
116:      *   255.0 — maximum 8-bit grayscale value (white).
117:      */
118:     private double[] backgroundNormalize(int[] gray, int width, int height, int tileSize) {
119:         int tilesX = (int) Math.ceil((double) width / tileSize);
120:         int tilesY = (int) Math.ceil((double) height / tileSize);
121: 
122:         // Sample background level per tile (95th percentile = bright, since text is dark)
123:         double[][] bgLevels = new double[tilesY][tilesX];
124:         for (int ty = 0; ty < tilesY; ty++) {
125:             for (int tx = 0; tx < tilesX; tx++) {
126:                 int startX = tx * tileSize;
127:                 int startY = ty * tileSize;
128:                 int endX = Math.min(startX + tileSize, width);
129:                 int endY = Math.min(startY + tileSize, height);
130:                 int count = (endX - startX) * (endY - startY);
131:                 int[] sorted = new int[count];
132:                 int idx = 0;
133:                 for (int y = startY; y < endY; y++) {
134:                     for (int x = startX; x < endX; x++) {
135:                         sorted[idx++] = gray[y * width + x];
136:                     }
137:                 }
138:                 java.util.Arrays.sort(sorted);
139:                 bgLevels[ty][tx] = sorted[(int) (count * percentile)];
140:             }
141:         }
142: 
143:         // Bilinear interpolation of background at each pixel
144:         double[] result = new double[gray.length];
145:         for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
146:             for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
147:                 float fx = (float) x / tileSize;
148:                 float fy = (float) y / tileSize;
149:                 int tx0 = Math.min((int) Math.floor(fx), tilesX - 1);
150:                 int tx1 = Math.min(tx0 + 1, tilesX - 1);
151:                 int ty0 = Math.min((int) Math.floor(fy), tilesY - 1);
152:                 int ty1 = Math.min(ty0 + 1, tilesY - 1);
153: 
154:                 double bg = bilinearInterp(
155:                         bgLevels[ty0][tx0], bgLevels[ty0][tx1],
156:                         bgLevels[ty1][tx0], bgLevels[ty1][tx1],
157:                         fx - tx0, fy - ty0);
158: 
159:                 int idx = y * width + x;
160:                 if (bg > 0) {
161:                     // Normalize: stretch so that bg -> 255
162:                     result[idx] = Math.min(255.0, gray[idx] * 255.0 / bg);
163:                 } else {
164:                     result[idx] = gray[idx];
165:                 }
166:             }
167:         }
168:         return result;
169:     }
170: 
171:     /**
172:      * Standard bilinear interpolation over a unit square [0,1]x[0,1].
173:      *
174:      *   v00 .. v11  — values at the four corners (top-left, top-right, bottom-left, bottom-right).
175:      *   fx, fy      — fractional offsets within the square (0..1).
176:      *
177:      * Interpolation is performed in two passes:
178:      *   1. Linearly interpolate horizontally between the top corners, and between the bottom corners.
179:      *   2. Linearly interpolate vertically between the two horizontal results.
180:      * This is equivalent to: v = (1-fy)*((1-fx)*v00 + fx*v01) + fy*((1-fx)*v10 + fx*v11)
181:      *
182:      * No magic numbers — pure linear algebra.
183:      */
184:     private double bilinearInterp(double v00, double v01, double v10, double v11, double fx, double fy) {
185:         double top = v00 + (v01 - v00) * fx;
186:         double bot = v10 + (v11 - v10) * fx;
187:         return top + (bot - top) * fy;
188:     }
189: 
190:     /**
191:      * Otsu's method for automatic image thresholding.
192:      *
193:      * Theory: exhaustively search all 256 possible threshold values and pick the
194:      * one that maximises the inter-class variance between foreground and background
195:      * pixel distributions.  This gives optimal separation without any user tuning.
196:      *
197:      * Algorithm steps:
198:      *   1. Build a 256-bin histogram of pixel intensities.
199:      *   2. For each threshold t (0..255), split pixels into two classes:
200:      *      class B (background, intensities > t) and class F (foreground, ≤ t).
201:      *   3. Compute the between-class variance:
202:      *          σ² = wB * wF * (μB - μF)²
203:      *      where w = weight (proportion of pixels), μ = mean intensity.
204:      *   4. Return the t that maximises σ².
205:      *
206:      * Magic numbers:
207:      *   256 — number of bins in an 8-bit grayscale histogram (2^8 possible values).
208:      *   wB, wF  — weights (class pixel counts).  These are integers but the formula
209:      *     uses them as the product to give heavier weight to balanced splits.
210:      */
211:     private int otsuThreshold(double[] pixels) {
212:         int[] histogram = new int[256];
213:         for (double p : pixels) {
214:             int val = Math.min(255, Math.max(0, (int) Math.round(p)));
215:             histogram[val]++;
216:         }
217: 
218:         int total = pixels.length;
219:         double sum = 0;
220:         for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
221:             sum += i * histogram[i];
222:         }
223: 
224:         double sumB = 0;
225:         int wB = 0;
226:         double maxVariance = 0;
227:         int threshold = 0;
228: 
229:         for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
230:             wB += histogram[i];
231:             if (wB == 0) continue;
232:             int wF = total - wB;
233:             if (wF == 0) break;
234: 
235:             sumB += i * histogram[i];
236:             double meanB = sumB / wB;
237:             double meanF = (sum - sumB) / wF;
238:             double variance = (double) wB * wF * (meanB - meanF) * (meanB - meanF);
239: 
240:             if (variance > maxVariance) {
241:                 maxVariance = variance;
242:                 threshold = i;
243:             }
244:         }
245:         return threshold;
246:     }
247: 
248:     /**
249:      * Simple inpainting: replace foreground (text) pixels with the nearest
250:      * background pixel colour found within a search radius.
251:      *
252:      * This produces a "cleaned" page where text regions are filled in with
253:      * the surrounding page colour — useful as a background layer for PDF
254:      * re-assembly (the text will be overlaid as an invisible OCR layer).
255:      *
256:      * Algorithm:
257:      *   For each pixel that the mask identifies as foreground (black):
258:      *     1. Search outward in a square (top-left to bottom-right) within radius.
259:      *     2. Pick the first background (white in mask) pixel found.
260:      *     3. Copy that pixel's colour to the result.
261:      *   Background pixels are copied unchanged.
262:      *
263:      * This is a crude "nearest neighbour" inpaint — a real implementation would
264:      * use a proper diffusion or patch-match algorithm, but this is sufficient
265:      * for the page-background use case.
266:      *
267:      * Magic numbers:
268:      *   radius — search window size (passed in as parameter; typically 3).
269:      *     3 is used because typical text stroke widths at 300 DPI are 2-4 px.
270:      *     Larger values handle thicker strokes but are slower.
271:      *   0xFFFFFF — bitmask to extract only the RGB channels, discarding alpha.
272:      *     setRGB expects full ARGB, so foreground is 0xFF000000 (black w/ alpha=FF)
273:      *     and background is 0xFFFFFFFF (white w/ alpha=FF).
274:      *   Bit shifts for colour reconstruction:
275:      *     (bestR << 16) | (bestG << 8) | bestB — packs R, G, B into 0x00RRGGBB.
276:      *     Alpha is also needed: | 0xFF000000 for full opacity.
277:      *     (nrgb >> 16) & 0xFF, (nrgb >> 8) & 0xFF, nrgb & 0xFF — extract
278:      *     individual 8-bit colour channels from a 32-bit ARGB int.
279:      */
280:     private BufferedImage inpaintBackground(BufferedImage original, BufferedImage mask, int radius) {
281:         int width = original.getWidth();
282:         int height = original.getHeight();
283:         BufferedImage result = new BufferedImage(width, height, BufferedImage.TYPE_INT_RGB);
284: 
285:         for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
286:             for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
287:                 int maskRgb = mask.getRGB(x, y);
288:                 boolean isForeground = (maskRgb & 0xFFFFFF) == 0;
289: 
290:                 if (!isForeground) {
291:                     result.setRGB(x, y, original.getRGB(x, y));
292:                 } else {
293:                     // Find nearest background pixel within radius
294:                     int bestR = 0, bestG = 0, bestB = 0;
295:                     int found = 0;
296:                     for (int dy = -radius; dy <= radius && found == 0; dy++) {
297:                         for (int dx = -radius; dx <= radius && found == 0; dx++) {
298:                             int nx = x + dx;
299:                             int ny = y + dy;
300:                             if (nx < 0 || nx >= width || ny < 0 || ny >= height) continue;
301:                             int nmask = mask.getRGB(nx, ny);
302:                             if ((nmask & 0xFFFFFF) != 0) {
303:                                 int nrgb = original.getRGB(nx, ny);
304:                                 bestR = (nrgb >> 16) & 0xFF;
305:                                 bestG = (nrgb >> 8) & 0xFF;
306:                                 bestB = nrgb & 0xFF;
307:                                 found++;
308:                             }
309:                         }
310:                     }
311:                     if (found > 0) {
312:                         int rgb = 0xFF000000 | (bestR << 16) | (bestG << 8) | bestB;
313:                         result.setRGB(x, y, rgb);
314:                     } else {
315:                         result.setRGB(x, y, original.getRGB(x, y));
316:                     }
317:                 }
318:             }
319:         }
320:         return result;
321:     }
322: }

(End of file - total 322 lines)
</content>

143:     }
144: 
145:     private void runPipeline(File inputFile, File outputFile,
146:                              ImageSegmenter segmenter,
147:                              OCREngine ocrEngine, JBIG2Compressor compressor,
148:                              PDFAssembler assembler, boolean useMrc, boolean usePdfa,
149:                              float dpi) throws IOException {
150: 
151:         // Create temp directory for this run's intermediate files
152:         String inputName = inputFile.getName().replaceAll("\\.pdf$", "");
153:         File tempDir = new File("temp/" + inputName + "-" + System.nanoTime());
154:         tempDir.mkdirs();
155: 
156:         try (PDDocument source = Loader.loadPDF(inputFile)) {
157:             PDFRenderer renderer = new PDFRenderer(source);
158:             int pageCount = source.getNumberOfPages();
159:             long totalStart = System.nanoTime();
160: 
161:             System.out.println("  Processing " + pageCount + " pages...");
162: 
163:             // ── Pass 1: extract, segment, OCR (streaming, one page at a time) ──
164:             List<PageResult> ocrResults = new ArrayList<>(pageCount);
165:             int[] imgWidths = new int[pageCount];
166:             int[] imgHeights = new int[pageCount];
167: 
168:             for (int i = 0; i < pageCount; i++) {
169:                 long t0 = System.nanoTime();
170: 
171:                 BufferedImage page = renderer.renderImageWithDPI(i, dpi);
172: 
173:                 // Convert to grayscale and save for OCR
174:                 BufferedImage gray = toGrayscale(page);
175:                 ImageIO.write(gray, "png", new File(tempDir, "page-" + i + ".png"));
176: 
177:                 imgWidths[i] = gray.getWidth();
178:                 imgHeights[i] = gray.getHeight();
179: 
180:                 BufferedImage background;
181:                 if (useMrc) {
182:                     SegmentedImage seg = segmenter.segment(page);
183:                     background = seg.getCleanedBackground();
184:                     // Save foreground mask for batch JBIG2
185:                     ImageIO.write(seg.getForegroundMask(), "png",
186:                         new File(tempDir, "mask-" + i + ".png"));
187:                 } else {
188:                     background = gray;
189:                 }
190: 
191:                 // Save background for assembly (re-read from disk in pass 2)
192:                 ImageIO.write(background, "png", new File(tempDir, "bg-" + i + ".png"));
193: 
194:                 // Release per-page images
195:                 page = null;
196:                 gray = null;
197:                 background = null;
198: 
199:                 // OCR from saved grayscale PNG
200:                 PageResult ocr = ocrEngine.ocr(i, tempDir);
201:                 ocrResults.add(ocr);
202: 
203:                 double elapsed = (System.nanoTime() - t0) / 1e9;
204:                 System.out.printf("    Page %3d: %.1fs%n", i + 1, elapsed);
205:             }
206: 
207:             // ── JBIG2 batch compression (shared dictionary across all pages) ──
208:             JBIG2Compressor.BatchResult jbig2Batch = null;
209:             if (useMrc && compressor != null) {
210:                 long t0 = System.nanoTime();
211:                 System.out.println("  Batch JBIG2 compression...");
212:                 jbig2Batch = compressor.compressAllFromDir(tempDir, pageCount, imgWidths, imgHeights);
213:                 double elapsed = (System.nanoTime() - t0) / 1e9;
214:                 if (jbig2Batch != null) {
215:                     System.out.printf("    JBIG2 batch done in %.1fs (sym: %d bytes)%n",
216:                         elapsed, jbig2Batch.getGlobalSym().length);
217:                 } else {
218:                     System.out.println("    JBIG2 unavailable — using CCITT G4 fallback");
219:                 }
220:             }
221: 
222:             // ── Pass 2: assemble (streaming) ──
223:             System.out.println("  Assembling PDF...");
224:             PDDocument output = new PDDocument();
225:             List<PDPage> outPages = new ArrayList<>(pageCount);
226: 
227:             for (int i = 0; i < pageCount; i++) {
228:                 BufferedImage bg = ImageIO.read(new File(tempDir, "bg-" + i + ".png"));
229: 
230:                 PDPage outPage;
231:                 if (jbig2Batch != null && jbig2Batch.getGlobalSym().length > 0) {
232:                     JBIG2Compressor.CompressionResult pageData = jbig2Batch.getPages().get(i);
233:                     outPage = assembler.addPageJbig2(output, source, i, bg,
234:                         pageData.getData(), jbig2Batch.getGlobalSym(),
235:                         pageData.getWidth(), pageData.getHeight(),
236:                         ocrResults.get(i));
237:                 } else if (useMrc) {
238:                     // CCITT G4 foreground (no shared JBIG2 available)
239:                     BufferedImage mask = ImageIO.read(new File(tempDir, "mask-" + i + ".png"));
240:                     outPage = assembler.addPage(output, source, i, bg, mask, ocrResults.get(i));
241:                     mask = null;
242:                 } else {
243:                     outPage = assembler.addPage(output, source, i, bg, null, ocrResults.get(i));
244:                 }
245: 
246:                 outPages.add(outPage);
247:                 bg = null;
248:             }
249: 
250:             // Finalize: copy metadata, add PDF/A if needed
251:             System.out.println("  Finalizing document...");
252:             assembler.finishAssembly(output, source, outPages, usePdfa);
253:             output.save(outputFile);
254: 
255:             long totalElapsed = (System.nanoTime() - totalStart) / 1_000_000_000L;
256:             System.out.printf("  Total: %d pages in %d:%02d%n", pageCount,
257:                     totalElapsed / 60, totalElapsed % 60);
258: 
259:         } finally {
260:             deleteDir(tempDir);
261:         }
262:     }
263: 
264:     private static BufferedImage toGrayscale(BufferedImage image) {
265:         if (image.getType() == BufferedImage.TYPE_BYTE_GRAY) return image;
266:         BufferedImage gray = new BufferedImage(image.getWidth(), image.getHeight(), BufferedImage.TYPE_BYTE_GRAY);
267:         Graphics2D g = gray.createGraphics();
268:         g.drawImage(image, 0, 0, null);
269:         g.dispose();
270:         return gray;
271:     }
272: 
273:     private static void deleteDir(File dir) {
274:         File[] files = dir.listFiles();
275:         if (files != null) {
276:             for (File f : files) {
277:                 if (f.isDirectory()) {
278:                     deleteDir(f);
279:                 }
280:                 f.delete();
281:             }
282:         }
283:         dir.delete();
284:     }
285: 
286:     public static void main(String[] args) {
287:         int exitCode = new CommandLine(new TrulyFreeOCR()).execute(args);
288:         System.exit(exitCode);
289:     }
290: }

110:         try (BufferedReader reader = new BufferedReader(new java.io.FileReader(tsv))) {
111:             String header = reader.readLine();
112:             if (header == null) return blocks;

132:                 } catch (NumberFormatException e) {
133:                 }
134:             }

88:      * with the {@code -p} flag, producing one shared symbol dictionary
89:      * and per-page JBIG2 streams.
90:      *
91:      * @param maskDir    Directory containing mask PNGs named {@code mask-0.png},
92:      *                   {@code mask-1.png}, ..., {@code mask-{pageCount-1}.png}.
93:      * @param pageCount  Number of masks / pages.
94:      * @param imgWidth   Width of each mask in pixels.
95:      * @param imgHeight  Height of each mask in pixels.
96:      * @return BatchResult with shared global sym and per-page data, or null if
97:      *         jbig2enc is unavailable or fails (caller should use CCITT fallback).
98:      */
99:     public BatchResult compressAllFromDir(File maskDir, int pageCount, int[] imgWidths, int[] imgHeights) throws IOException {
100:         File jbig2enc = findJbig2enc();
101:         if (jbig2enc == null) return null;
102: 
103:         List<String> pngPaths = new ArrayList<>(pageCount);
104:         for (int i = 0; i < pageCount; i++) {
105:             pngPaths.add(new File(maskDir, "mask-" + i + ".png").getAbsolutePath());
106:         }
107: 
108:         // Use the first mask file's path (without .png) as the basename so that
109:         // jbig2enc writes deterministic output files alongside the masks:
110:         //   <basename>.sym  — shared global symbol dictionary
111:         //   <basename>.0000, <basename>.0001, ... — per-page JBIG2 data
112:         String firstPng = pngPaths.get(0);
113:         String basename = firstPng.replaceAll("\\.png$", "");
114: 
115:         String flags = Settings.getInstance().getString("jbig2enc.flags", "-p -s");
116:         List<String> args = new ArrayList<>();
117:         for (String f : flags.split("\\s+")) {
118:             if (!f.isEmpty()) args.add(f);
119:         }
120:         args.add("-b");
121:         args.add(basename);
122:         args.addAll(pngPaths);
123: 
124:         SubprocessRunner.Result result = SubprocessRunner.run(jbig2enc, args, -1);
125:         if (result.getExitCode() != 0) return null;
126: 
127:         // Read shared global symbol dictionary
128:         File symFile = new File(basename + ".sym");
129:         byte[] globalSym = symFile.exists() ? Files.readAllBytes(symFile.toPath()) : new byte[0];

131: 
132:         // Read per-page data (jbig2enc -p writes <basename>.0000, .0001, ...)

136:             byte[] pageData = pageFile.exists() ? Files.readAllBytes(pageFile.toPath()) : new byte[0];
137:             pages.add(new CompressionResult(pageData, imgWidths[i], imgHeights[i], true));
138:         }
139: 
140:         return new BatchResult(globalSym, pages);

142: 
143:     /**
144:      * Attempts JBIG2 compression via jbig2enc; falls back to CCITT G4 on failure.
145:      *
146:      * @param foregroundMask  Binary image (TYPE_BYTE_BINARY, black=foreground).
147:      * @return CompressionResult with either JBIG2 or CCITT G4 data.
148:      */
149:     public CompressionResult compress(BufferedImage foregroundMask) throws IOException {
150:         File jbig2enc = findJbig2enc();
151:         if (jbig2enc != null) {
152:             try {

154:             } catch (IOException e) {

157:         }

161:     /**

163:      *
164:      * Searches native/{os}/jbig2enc (or jbig2enc.exe on Windows).
165:      * The base path can be overridden via system property "tfocr.native.dir"
166:      * (defaults to "native").
167:      *
168:      * @return The executable File, or null if not found.
169:      */
170:     private File findJbig2enc() {
171:         Os os = PlatformUtils.detectOs();
172:         String dirName;
173:         switch (os) {
174:             case WINDOWS: dirName = "win"; break;
175:             case MAC: dirName = "mac"; break;
176:             default: dirName = "linux";
177:         }
178:         File exe = new File(nativeDir + "/" + dirName, os == Os.WINDOWS ? "jbig2enc.exe" : "jbig2enc");
179:         if (exe.canExecute()) return exe;
180:         return null;
181:     }
182: 
183:     /**
184:      * Runs jbig2enc and concatenates global sym + page jbig2 into one byte array.
185:      *
186:      * PDF JBIG2Decode streams require global segments (symbol dictionary)
187:      * followed by page data — exactly the .sym + .jbig2 layout that
188:      * jbig2enc produces.
189:      */
190:     private CompressionResult compressWithJbig2enc(File jbig2enc, BufferedImage mask) throws IOException {
191:         File tempPng = File.createTempFile("tfocr-jbig2-", ".png");
192:         tempPng.deleteOnExit();
193:         javax.imageio.ImageIO.write(mask, "png", tempPng);
194: 
195:         try {
196:             String prefix = tempPng.getAbsolutePath().replaceAll("\\.png$", "");
197: 
198:             String flags = Settings.getInstance().getString("jbig2enc.flags", "-p -s");
199:             java.util.List<String> args = new java.util.ArrayList<>();
200:             for (String f : flags.split("\\s+")) {
201:                 if (!f.isEmpty()) args.add(f);
202:             }
203:             args.add("-b");
204:             args.add(prefix);
205:             args.add(tempPng.getAbsolutePath());
206: 
207:             SubprocessRunner.Result result = SubprocessRunner.run(jbig2enc, args, -1);
208:             if (result.getExitCode() != 0) {
209:                 throw new IOException("jbig2enc failed: " + result.getStderrString());
210:             }
211: 
212:             // With -p flag, jbig2enc produces <prefix>.sym + <prefix>.0000
213:             File symFile = new File(prefix + ".sym");
214:             File pageFile = new File(prefix + ".0000");
215: 
216:             byte[] symData = symFile.exists() ? java.nio.file.Files.readAllBytes(symFile.toPath()) : new byte[0];
217:             byte[] pageData = pageFile.exists() ? java.nio.file.Files.readAllBytes(pageFile.toPath()) : new byte[0];
218: 
219:             byte[] combined = new byte[symData.length + pageData.length];
220:             System.arraycopy(symData, 0, combined, 0, symData.length);
221:             System.arraycopy(pageData, 0, combined, symData.length, pageData.length);
222: 
223:             return new CompressionResult(combined, mask.getWidth(), mask.getHeight(), true);
224:         } finally {

226:             for (String ext : new String[]{".png", ".sym", ".0000"}) {
227:                 File f = new File(prefix + ext);
228:                 if (f.exists()) f.delete();
229:             }
230:         }
231:     }
232: 
233:     /**
234:      * Fallback: encodes the mask as CCITT Group 4 fax using PDFBox's CCITTFactory.
235:      */
236:     private CompressionResult compressWithFallback(BufferedImage mask) throws IOException {

238:         try (PDDocument doc = new PDDocument()) {

240:             return new CompressionResult(extractStreamBytes(ccitt), mask.getWidth(), mask.getHeight(), false);
241:         }
242:     }
243: 
244:     private static byte[] extractStreamBytes(PDImageXObject image) throws IOException {
245:         try (java.io.InputStream is = image.createInputStream()) {
246:             return is.readAllBytes();
247:         }
248:     }
249: }

31: import com.trulyfreeocr.model.PageResult;
32: import com.trulyfreeocr.model.TextBlock;
33: import com.trulyfreeocr.util.Settings;
34: 
35: /**
36:  * Re-assembles a searchable PDF from per-page inputs:
37:  *   - Source PDF (copied for page dimensions / media boxes)
38:  *   - Cleaned background images
39:  *   - Binary foreground masks (CCITT G4 compressed stencil overlay)
40:  *   - OCR results (invisible text layer)
41:  *
42:  * MRC-like layout (per page):
43:  *   1. Background layer: cleaned page image (Lossless PNG for now).
44:  *   2. Foreground mask: CCITT G4 compressed binary mask, drawn as a
45:  *      PDF ImageMask stencil in black — reveals only the text pixels
46:  *      on top of the background.
47:  *   3. Text layer: invisible OCR text (RenderingMode.NEITHER = Tr 3),
48:  *      selectable and searchable but not visible.
49:  *
50:  * Rendering mode NEITHER makes text invisible on screen/print while
51:  * keeping it selectable and searchable.
52:  *
53:  * Coordinate transformation:
54:  *   Page images at 300 DPI → PDF user space at 72 DPI.
55:  *   scaleX = pageWidth_pts  / imageWidth_px
56:  *   scaleY = pageHeight_pts / imageHeight_px
57:  *   Y is flipped: image origin is top-left, PDF origin is bottom-left.
58:  */
59: public class PDFAssembler {
60: 
61:     private final PDType1Font font;
62:     private final float minFontSize;
63:     private final MetadataPreserver preserver = new MetadataPreserver();
64:     private File pdfaFontFile;
65:     private JBIG2Compressor compressor;
66:     private COSStream cachedJbig2Globals;
67: 
68:     public PDFAssembler() {
69:         this("HELVETICA", 1f);
70:     }
71: 
72:     public PDFAssembler(String fontName, float minFontSize) {
73:         Standard14Fonts.FontName resolved;
74:         try {
75:             resolved = Standard14Fonts.FontName.valueOf(fontName);
76:         } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
77:             resolved = Standard14Fonts.FontName.HELVETICA;
78:         }
79:         this.font = new PDType1Font(resolved);
80:         this.minFontSize = minFontSize;
81:     }
82: 
83:     public void setPdfaFont(File fontFile) {
84:         this.pdfaFontFile = fontFile;
85:     }
86: 
87:     public void setCompressor(JBIG2Compressor compressor) {
88:         this.compressor = compressor;
89:     }
90: 
91:     /**
92:      * Builds a searchable PDF with MRC-like foreground mask overlay.
93:      *
94:      * When foregroundMasks is provided, each mask is CCITT G4 compressed
95:      * and drawn as a PDF ImageMask stencil in black on top of the background.
96:      * This reproduces the original text pixels at full sharpness, while
97:      * the background layer carries the cleaned (de-speckled) page image.
98:      *
99:      * @param sourcePdf       Original PDF (for per-page media boxes).
100:      * @param backgrounds     Per-page cleaned background images.
101:      * @param foregroundMasks Per-page binary foreground masks (TYPE_BYTE_BINARY,
102:      *                        black=text, white=background), or null to skip.
103:      * @param ocrResults      Per-page OCR results.
104:      * @param usePdfa         Enable PDF/A-2b output with XMP metadata.
105:      * @return A new PDDocument with foreground mask overlay and searchable text.
106:      */
107:     public PDDocument assemble(File sourcePdf,
108:                                List<BufferedImage> backgrounds,
109:                                List<BufferedImage> foregroundMasks,
110:                                List<PageResult> ocrResults,
111:                                boolean usePdfa) throws IOException {
112:         PDDocument output = new PDDocument();
113:         List<PDPage> outPages = new java.util.ArrayList<>();
114: 
115:         try (PDDocument source = Loader.loadPDF(sourcePdf)) {
116:             int pageCount = source.getNumberOfPages();
117:             for (int i = 0; i < pageCount; i++) {
118:                 BufferedImage bg = backgrounds.get(i);
119:                 BufferedImage fg = foregroundMasks != null ? foregroundMasks.get(i) : null;
120:                 PDPage page = addPage(output, source, i, bg, fg, ocrResults.get(i));
121:                 outPages.add(page);
122:             }
123:             finishAssembly(output, source, outPages, usePdfa);
124:         }
125: 
126:         return output;
127:     }
128: 
129:     /**
130:      * Renders one page into the output document.  Call repeatedly for
131:      * each page of the source, then call {@link #finishAssembly}.
132:      *
133:      * @param output        The output PDDocument being built.
134:      * @param source        The source PDDocument (already loaded).
135:      * @param pageIndex     0-based page index in source.
136:      * @param background    Cleaned background image for this page.
137:      * @param foregroundMask Binary mask or null to skip the stencil layer.
138:      * @param ocr           OCR result for this page.
139:      * @return The newly created PDPage added to output.
140:      */
141:     public PDPage addPage(PDDocument output, PDDocument source, int pageIndex,
142:                           BufferedImage background, BufferedImage foregroundMask,
143:                           PageResult ocr) throws IOException {
144:         PDPage sourcePage = source.getPage(pageIndex);
145:         PDRectangle mediaBox = sourcePage.getMediaBox();
146:         float pageW = mediaBox.getWidth();
147:         float pageH = mediaBox.getHeight();
148: 
149:         PDPage outPage = new PDPage(mediaBox);
150:         output.addPage(outPage);
151: 
152:         try (PDPageContentStream cs = new PDPageContentStream(output, outPage)) {
153:             // Layer 1: background image
154:             PDImageXObject bgXObject;
155:             if (foregroundMask == null) {
156:                 bgXObject = JPEGFactory.createFromImage(output, background, 0.85f);
157:             } else {
158:                 bgXObject = LosslessFactory.createFromImage(output, background);
159:             }
160:             cs.drawImage(bgXObject, 0, 0, pageW, pageH);
161: 
162:             // Layer 2: foreground mask as CCITT G4 stencil overlay (JBIG2 when available)
163:             if (foregroundMask != null) {
164:                 PDImageXObject fgImage;
165:                 if (compressor != null) {
166:                     JBIG2Compressor.CompressionResult result = compressor.compress(foregroundMask);
167:                     if (result.isJbig2()) {
168:                         fgImage = createJbig2ImageXObject(output, result);
169:                     } else {
170:                         fgImage = CCITTFactory.createFromImage(output, foregroundMask);
171:                     }
172:                 } else {
173:                     fgImage = CCITTFactory.createFromImage(output, foregroundMask);
174:                 }
175:                 fgImage.getCOSObject().setBoolean(COSName.IMAGE_MASK, true);
176:                 fgImage.getCOSObject().removeItem(COSName.COLORSPACE);
177:                 cs.setNonStrokingColor(0f, 0f, 0f);
178:                 cs.drawImage(fgImage, 0, 0, pageW, pageH);
179:             }
180: 
181:             // Layer 3: invisible OCR text
182:             float scaleX = pageW / ocr.getWidth();
183:             float scaleY = pageH / ocr.getHeight();
184:             PDFont pageFont = (pdfaFontFile != null && pdfaFontFile.exists())
185:                     ? PDType0Font.load(output, pdfaFontFile)
186:                     : font;
187:             cs.beginText();
188:             cs.setFont(pageFont, minFontSize);
189:             cs.setRenderingMode(RenderingMode.NEITHER);
190: 
191:             for (TextBlock tb : ocr.getTextBlocks()) {
192:                 float x = tb.getBbox().x * scaleX;
193:                 float y = pageH - (tb.getBbox().y + tb.getBbox().height) * scaleY;
194:                 float fontSize = Math.max(tb.getBbox().height * scaleY, minFontSize);
195:                 cs.setFont(pageFont, fontSize);
196:                 cs.setTextMatrix(Matrix.getTranslateInstance(x, y));
197:                 cs.showText(tb.getWord());
198:             }
199:             cs.endText();
200:         }
201: 
202:         return outPage;
203:     }
204: 
205:     /**
206:      * Copies metadata from the source and optionally adds PDF/A-2b info.
207:      * Must be called after all {@link #addPage} calls are complete.
208:      */
209:     public void finishAssembly(PDDocument output, PDDocument source,
210:                                List<PDPage> outPages, boolean usePdfa) throws IOException {
211:         preserver.preserve(source, output, outPages);
212:         if (usePdfa) {
213:             addPdfaMetadata(output);
214:         }
215:     }
216: 
217:     private PDImageXObject createJbig2ImageXObject(PDDocument doc, JBIG2Compressor.CompressionResult result) throws IOException {
218:         PDImageXObject img = new PDImageXObject(doc);
219:         img.setWidth(result.getWidth());
220:         img.setHeight(result.getHeight());
221:         img.setBitsPerComponent(1);
222:         img.setStencil(true);
223:         try (OutputStream os = img.getStream().createOutputStream()) {
224:             os.write(result.getData());
225:         }
226:         img.getCOSObject().setItem(COSName.FILTER, COSName.JBIG2_DECODE);
227:         return img;
228:     }
229: 
230:     private PDImageXObject createJbig2ImageXObject(PDDocument doc,
231:                                                    byte[] pageData,
232:                                                    byte[] globalSym,
233:                                                    int width,
234:                                                    int height) throws IOException {
235:         PDImageXObject img = new PDImageXObject(doc);
236:         img.setWidth(width);
237:         img.setHeight(height);
238:         img.setBitsPerComponent(1);
239:         img.setStencil(true);
240: 
241:         // Write per-page JBIG2 data (no filter pipeline — raw bytes are already compressed)
242:         try (OutputStream os = img.getStream().createOutputStream()) {
243:             os.write(pageData);
244:         }
245:         img.getCOSObject().setItem(COSName.FILTER, COSName.JBIG2_DECODE);
246: 
247:         // Create the shared global symbol dictionary stream ONCE and cache it.
248:         // Reusing the same COSStream reference for every PDImageXObject avoids
249:         // embedding N copies of the identical global dictionary in the PDF.
250:         if (cachedJbig2Globals == null) {
251:             cachedJbig2Globals = doc.getDocument().createCOSStream();
252:             try (OutputStream os = cachedJbig2Globals.createOutputStream()) {
253:                 os.write(globalSym);
254:             }
255:         }
256:         img.getCOSObject().setItem(COSName.JBIG2_GLOBALS, cachedJbig2Globals);
257: 
258:         return img;
259:     }
260: 
261:     /**
262:      * Adds one page to the output document using pre-compressed JBIG2
263:      * foreground data with a shared global symbol dictionary.
264:      */
265:     public PDPage addPageJbig2(PDDocument output, PDDocument source, int pageIndex,
266:                                BufferedImage background,
267:                                byte[] jbig2PageData, byte[] jbig2GlobalSym,
268:                                int fgWidth, int fgHeight,
269:                                PageResult ocr) throws IOException {
270:         PDPage sourcePage = source.getPage(pageIndex);
271:         PDRectangle mediaBox = sourcePage.getMediaBox();
272:         float pageW = mediaBox.getWidth();
273:         float pageH = mediaBox.getHeight();
274: 
275:         PDPage outPage = new PDPage(mediaBox);
276:         output.addPage(outPage);
277: 
278:         try (PDPageContentStream cs = new PDPageContentStream(output, outPage)) {
279:             // Layer 1: background image
280:             PDImageXObject bgXObject = LosslessFactory.createFromImage(output, background);
281:             cs.drawImage(bgXObject, 0, 0, pageW, pageH);
282: 
283:             // Layer 2: JBIG2 foreground mask with shared globals
284:             if (jbig2PageData != null && jbig2GlobalSym != null) {
285:                 PDImageXObject fgImage = createJbig2ImageXObject(output,
286:                     jbig2PageData, jbig2GlobalSym, fgWidth, fgHeight);
287:                 fgImage.getCOSObject().setBoolean(COSName.IMAGE_MASK, true);
288:                 fgImage.getCOSObject().removeItem(COSName.COLORSPACE);
289:                 cs.setNonStrokingColor(0f, 0f, 0f);
290:                 cs.drawImage(fgImage, 0, 0, pageW, pageH);
291:             }
292: 
293:             // Layer 3: invisible OCR text
294:             float scaleX = pageW / ocr.getWidth();
295:             float scaleY = pageH / ocr.getHeight();
296:             PDFont pageFont = (pdfaFontFile != null && pdfaFontFile.exists())
297:                     ? PDType0Font.load(output, pdfaFontFile)
298:                     : font;
299:             cs.beginText();
300:             cs.setFont(pageFont, minFontSize);
301:             cs.setRenderingMode(RenderingMode.NEITHER);
302: 
303:             for (TextBlock tb : ocr.getTextBlocks()) {
304:                 float x = tb.getBbox().x * scaleX;
305:                 float y = pageH - (tb.getBbox().y + tb.getBbox().height) * scaleY;
306:                 float fontSize = Math.max(tb.getBbox().height * scaleY, minFontSize);
307:                 cs.setFont(pageFont, fontSize);
308:                 cs.setTextMatrix(Matrix.getTranslateInstance(x, y));
309:                 cs.showText(tb.getWord());
310:             }
311:             cs.endText();
312:         }
313: 
314:         return outPage;
315:     }
316: 
317:     private void addPdfaMetadata(PDDocument doc) throws IOException {
318:         PDDocumentCatalog catalog = doc.getDocumentCatalog();
319: 
320:         // PDF/A-2b XMP metadata
321:         String xmp = """
322:                 <?xpacket begin="\\uFEFF" id="W5M0MpCehiHzreSzNTczkc9d"?>
323:                 <x:xmpmeta xmlns:x="adobe:ns:meta/">
324:                   <rdf:RDF xmlns:rdf="http://www.w3.org/1999/02/22-rdf-syntax-ns#">

## 1. getRGB/setRGB pixel-by-pixel

**File:** `/home/bgu/GitHub/msmarkgu/TrulyFreeOCR/src/main/java/com/trulyfreeocr/pipeline/ImageSegmenter.java`

There are **2 distinct methods** in the main source code that use `getRGB()`/`setRGB()` in nested pixel loops:

### A. `toGrayscale()` -- 1 call to `getRGB` in a nested pixel loop

| Line | Call | Context |
|------|------|---------|
| **84** | `image.getRGB(x, y)` | Inside `for (int y = 0; y < height; y++)` / `for (int x = 0; x < width; x++)` |

```java
// Lines 82-90
for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
    for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
        int rgb = image.getRGB(x, y);      // <-- 1 getRGB call per pixel
        int r = (rgb >> 16) & 0xFF;
        int g = (rgb >> 8) & 0xFF;
        int b = rgb & 0xFF;
        gray[y * width + x] = (int) (0.299 * r + 0.587 * g + 0.114 * b);
    }
}
```

**Total getRGB calls per invocation:** `width * height` (every pixel once). **No setRGB calls here.**

### B. `segment()` (the Otsu binarization step) -- 2 calls to `setRGB` in a nested pixel loop

| Line | Call | Context |
|------|------|---------|
| **49** | `foregroundMask.setRGB(x, y, 0xFF000000)` | Inside `for (int y = 0; y < height; y++)` / `for (int x = 0; x < width; x++)` -- writing black for foreground |
| **51** | `foregroundMask.setRGB(x, y, 0xFFFFFFFF)` | Same loop -- writing white for background |

```java
// Lines 43-54
for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
    for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
        int idx = y * width + x;
        if (gray[idx] <= threshold) {
            foregroundMask.setRGB(x, y, 0xFF000000); // <-- setRGB per pixel
        } else {
            foregroundMask.setRGB(x, y, 0xFFFFFFFF); // <-- setRGB per pixel
        }
    }
}
```

**Total setRGB calls per invocation:** `width * height` (every pixel, exactly once).

### C. `inpaintBackground()` -- 5 calls to getRGB + 3 calls to setRGB in nested pixel loops

| Line | Call | Context |
|------|------|---------|
| **287** | `mask.getRGB(x, y)` | Outer pixel loop (every pixel) |
| **291** | `result.setRGB(x, y, original.getRGB(x, y))` | Background pixels (direct copy) |
| **291** (inner) | `original.getRGB(x, y)` | Same line -- inside setRGB argument |
| **301** | `mask.getRGB(nx, ny)` | Inner search loop (within `radius`) |
| **303** | `original.getRGB(nx, ny)` | Inner search loop |
| **313** | `result.setRGB(x, y, rgb)` | Foreground pixels (reconstructed) |
| **315** | `result.setRGB(x, y, original.getRGB(x, y))` | Fallback (no neighbor found) |

```java
// Lines 285-319
for (int y = 0; y < height; y++) {
    for (int x = 0; x < width; x++) {
        int maskRgb = mask.getRGB(x, y);                              // getRGB call 1 (every pixel)
        boolean isForeground = (maskRgb & 0xFFFFFF) == 0;

        if (!isForeground) {
            result.setRGB(x, y, original.getRGB(x, y));               // setRGB call + getRGB call (background)
        } else {
            int bestR = 0, bestG = 0, bestB = 0;
            int found = 0;
            for (int dy = -radius; dy <= radius && found == 0; dy++) {
                for (int dx = -radius; dx <= radius && found == 0; dx++) {
                    int nx = x + dx;
                    int ny = y + dy;
                    if (nx < 0 || nx >= width || ny < 0 || ny >= height) continue;
                    int nmask = mask.getRGB(nx, ny);                  // getRGB call (search loop)
                    if ((nmask & 0xFFFFFF) != 0) {
                        int nrgb = original.getRGB(nx, ny);           // getRGB call (search loop)
                        bestR = (nrgb >> 16) & 0xFF;
                        bestG = (nrgb >> 8) & 0xFF;
                        bestB = nrgb & 0xFF;
                        found++;
                    }
                }
            }
            if (found > 0) {
                int rgb = 0xFF000000 | (bestR << 16) | (bestG << 8) | bestB;
                result.setRGB(x, y, rgb);                              // setRGB call (foreground)
            } else {
                result.setRGB(x, y, original.getRGB(x, y));           // setRGB call + getRGB call (fallback)
            }
        }
    }
}
```

**Total per invocation:** 
- `getRGB`: `width * height` (outer) + `foreground_count * (2 * radius)^2` (search loop) = up to `W*H + (W*H) * 49` with radius=3
- `setRGB`: `width * height` (every pixel gets written exactly once)

### Summary counts (main source only, ImageSegmenter.java):

| Method | `getRGB` calls | `setRGB` calls | Nested pixel loops? |
|--------|---------------|---------------|---------------------|
| `toGrayscale()` (line 77) | 1 (line 84) | 0 | Yes (line 82-83) |
| `segment()` (line 30) | 0 | 2 (lines 49, 51) | Yes (line 43-44) |
| `inpaintBackground()` (line 280) | 3+ (lines 287, 291, 301, 303, 315) | 3 (lines 291, 313, 315) | Yes (line 285-286 + 296-297) |

**Verdict: The concern is valid.** Every pixel in 3 separate methods goes through slow `getRGB()`/`setRGB()` calls. The `toGrayscale()` and `segment()` sections touch every pixel exactly once per pixel. `inpaintBackground()` is the worst: it calls `getRGB` for every pixel in the outer loop, and for foreground pixels it can call `getRGB` up to `(2*radius+1)^2 = 49` times in the inner search loop. This is a significant performance hotspot for high-resolution pages.

## 2. PNG vs BMP/TIFF

### All `ImageIO.write(... "png" ...)` calls in main source:

**File:** `/home/bgu/GitHub/msmarkgu/TrulyFreeOCR/src/main/java/com/trulyfreeocr/TrulyFreeOCR.java`

| Line | Code | What is written |
|------|------|----------------|
| **175** | `ImageIO.write(gray, "png", new File(tempDir, "page-" + i + ".png"))` | Grayscale page image for OCR |
| **185-186** | `ImageIO.write(seg.getForegroundMask(), "png", new File(tempDir, "mask-" + i + ".png"))` | Binary foreground mask |
| **192** | `ImageIO.write(background, "png", new File(tempDir, "bg-" + i + ".png"))` | Cleaned background image |

| Line | Code | What is written |
|------|------|----------------|
| **193** | `javax.imageio.ImageIO.write(mask, "png", tempPng)` | Temporary mask PNG for jbig2enc input |

**Total main-source PNG writes: 4 per page** (3 in TrulyFreeOCR.java, 1 in JBIG2Compressor.java). That is **4 disk writes to PNG per page** in the main pipeline.

### Does Tesseract CLI accept BMP/TIFF input?

**File:** `/home/bgu/GitHub/msmarkgu/TrulyFreeOCR/src/main/java/com/trulyfreeocr/pipeline/OCREngine.java`

```java
// Lines 56-63
ProcessBuilder pb = new ProcessBuilder(
        tesseractPath,
        pngFile.getAbsolutePath(),   // <-- input file
        prefix,                      // output prefix (strips .png)
        "-l", language,
        "--psm", psm,
        "tsv"
);
```

The Tesseract command is invoked as:
```
tesseract <pngFile> <prefix> -l <lang> --psm <psm> tsv
```

Tesseract's CLI **does not care about the file extension**. You can pass it any image format it supports (PNG, TIFF, BMP, JPEG, etc.) and it will read it. The code just so happens to use `.png` files. It could pass a `.tiff` or `.bmp` file with no code changes to the Tesseract invocation.

### Does jbig2enc accept BMP/TIFF input?

**File:** `/home/bgu/GitHub/msmarkgu/TrulyFreeOCR/src/main/java/com/trulyfreeocr/pipeline/JBIG2Compressor.java`

```java
// Lines 113, 191-193
String basename = firstPng.replaceAll("\\.png$", "");     // strips .png from basename
...
File tempPng = File.createTempFile("tfocr-jbig2-", ".png");  // always uses .png
javax.imageio.ImageIO.write(mask, "png", tempPng);           // writes PNG
...
args.add(tempPng.getAbsolutePath());                         // passes to jbig2enc
```

The batch path (lines 104-105) also constructs PNG paths:
```java
pngPaths.add(new File(maskDir, "mask-" + i + ".png").getAbsolutePath());
```

**jbig2enc** (like Tesseract) takes whatever image format you give it. It reads the image header to determine format -- it does not rely on the file extension. It supports PNG, TIFF, BMP, etc. The code hardcodes PNG but could pass any format.

**Verdict: The concern is valid but the scope is limited.** All 4 disk writes per page use PNG (lossless). Switching to an uncompressed format like BMP would eliminate PNG compression/decompression overhead at the cost of larger disk I/O. TIFF would also dodge the PNG compression step. Both Tesseract and jbig2enc accept BMP/TIFF at the CLI level -- no command-line changes needed, you would only need to change the `ImageIO.write(..., "png", ...)` format string and the file extension.

## 3. Sequential loop

**File:** `/home/bgu/GitHub/msmarkgu/TrulyFreeOCR/src/main/java/com/trulyfreeocr/TrulyFreeOCR.java`

### The main processing loop (the "Pass 1" loop over pages):

```java
// Lines 168-205
for (int i = 0; i < pageCount; i++) {          // <-- SEQUENTIAL for loop
    long t0 = System.nanoTime();

    BufferedImage page = renderer.renderImageWithDPI(i, dpi);
    BufferedImage gray = toGrayscale(page);
    ImageIO.write(gray, "png", new File(tempDir, "page-" + i + ".png"));

    // ... segmentation, background cleaning, ImageIO writes ...

    PageResult ocr = ocrEngine.ocr(i, tempDir);  // Tesseract subprocess
    ocrResults.add(ocr);

    double elapsed = (System.nanoTime() - t0) / 1e9;
    System.out.printf("    Page %3d: %.1fs%n", i + 1, elapsed);
}
```

### The "Pass 2" assembly loop:

```java
// Lines 227-248
for (int i = 0; i < pageCount; i++) {           // <-- SEQUENTIAL for loop
    BufferedImage bg = ImageIO.read(new File(tempDir, "bg-" + i + ".png"));
    // ... assembly ...
}
```

**Both loops are strictly sequential single-threaded for loops.** There is no `ExecutorService`, no `parallelStream()`, no `CompletableFuture`, no thread pool submission.

### Was concurrency removed?

There is **no evidence that concurrency was ever present and then removed**. There are no commented-out concurrency calls, no `parallel()` stream calls, no `executor.submit()` patterns. However, note the CLI option on line 69-70:

```java
@Option(names = {"--threads"}, description = "Threads for segmentation (default: # CPUs). OCR limited to pipeline.ocr.maxThreads (default 1).")
private Integer threads;
```

This `threads` field exists as a CLI option but is **never read or used** anywhere in the `call()` or `runPipeline()` method. It was apparently planned/intended for future use or was part of an earlier design but was never wired in. The `--threads` option is declared but completely dead code.

**Verdict: The concern is correct.** Page processing is entirely sequential. The `--threads` option exists but is never referenced in the pipeline logic -- it is dead code. Each page is rendered, segmented, OCR'd, and assembled one at a time with no parallelism. The per-page timing output (`Page %3d: %.1fs`) shows the sequential nature clearly.

## 4. Otsu floating point

**File:** `/home/bgu/GitHub/msmarkgu/TrulyFreeOCR/src/main/java/com/trulyfreeocr/pipeline/ImageSegmenter.java`

### The `otsuThreshold` method (lines 211-246):

```java
private int otsuThreshold(double[] pixels) {
    int[] histogram = new int[256];
    for (double p : pixels) {
        int val = Math.min(255, Math.max(0, (int) Math.round(p)));  // <-- Line 214
        histogram[val]++;
    }

    int total = pixels.length;
    double sum = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
        sum += i * histogram[i];
    }

    double sumB = 0;
    int wB = 0;
    double maxVariance = 0;
    int threshold = 0;

    for (int i = 0; i < 256; i++) {
        wB += histogram[i];
        if (wB == 0) continue;
        int wF = total - wB;
        if (wF == 0) break;

        sumB += i * histogram[i];
        double meanB = sumB / wB;
        double meanF = (sum - sumB) / wF;
        double variance = (double) wB * wF * (meanB - meanF) * (meanB - meanF);  // <-- Line 238

        if (variance > maxVariance) {
            maxVariance = variance;
            threshold = i;
        }
    }
    return threshold;
}
```

The **only line with Math.min/Math.max/Math.round** is **line 214**:
```java
int val = Math.min(255, Math.max(0, (int) Math.round(p)));
```

This is used to clamp the `double` pixel value to a valid `[0, 255]` integer bin index for the histogram. The method accepts `double[] pixels` because the input comes from `backgroundNormalize()` which returns `double[]` (normalized floating-point values). 

However, there is a subtle inefficiency here: **the double array is entirely unnecessary**. The background normalization step produces `double[]` values, but the Otsu method immediately bins them into a 256-bin integer histogram. The `Math.round()` + `Math.min/Math.max` overhead is incurred for every single pixel. If `backgroundNormalize` returned `int[]` instead (clamped to 0-255), the Otsu method could skip the floating-point clamping entirely and just do `histogram[p]++`.

**Verdict: The concern is partially valid.** The `(int) Math.round(p)` + `Math.min(255, Math.max(0, ...))` per pixel adds overhead, and the use of `double` throughout when the end result is always a 256-bin integer histogram is indeed wasteful. However, this is a minor cost compared to the pixel-loop getRGB/setRGB issues. The floating-point variance computation on line 238 is actually fine -- it operates on the 256-element histogram, not per-pixel, so its cost is negligible.

---

## 5. Tesseract command args (bonus)

**File:** `/home/bgu/GitHub/msmarkgu/TrulyFreeOCR/src/main/java/com/trulyfreeocr/pipeline/OCREngine.java`, lines 56-63:

```java
ProcessBuilder pb = new ProcessBuilder(
        tesseractPath,
        pngFile.getAbsolutePath(),           // <-- input image
        prefix,                              // <-- output prefix (dir + "page-N")
        "-l", language,                      // <-- language (e.g. "eng")
        "--psm", psm,                        // <-- page seg mode (e.g. "1")
        "tsv"                                // <-- output format: TSV
);
```

The Tesseract CLI invocation is:
```
tesseract <input_image> <output_prefix> -l <lang> --psm <mode> tsv
```

For example:
```
tesseract /tmp/temp123/page-0.png /tmp/temp123/page-0 -l eng --psm 1 tsv
```

This creates a TSV file at `/tmp/temp123/page-0.tsv`.

**Input format expectations:** Tesseract's `tesseract` binary auto-detects the image format from the file header. It supports PNG, TIFF, BMP, JPEG, PNM, etc. **There is no format restriction at the command line.** The `.png` extension is just a convention in this codebase -- you could pass a `.bmp` or `.tiff` file and Tesseract would handle it identically.

**Timeout:** 120 seconds hard-coded (line 78), with forced destruction on timeout.

<summary>Thinking</summary>

The exploration shows all 4 suggestions are valid. Let me now verify a few things more specifically to answer the user's question about whether the suggestions "make sense":

1. **getRGB bulk access** — Definitely valid. `ImageSegmenter.java` calls `getRGB(x, y)` in nested loops in `toGrayscale()` (line 84, once per pixel) and `setRGB(x, y, ...)` in `segment()` (lines 49, 51, once per pixel). `inpaintBackground()` is the worst with up to 49 getRGB calls per foreground pixel. Bulk `image.getRGB(0, 0, w, h, int[], 0, w)` would be much faster.

2. **PNG → BMP/TIFF** — Valid. 4 `ImageIO.write("png")` calls per page. Tesseract and jbig2enc auto-detect image format from headers. However, there's a subtle issue: `OCREngine.ocr(int pageIndex, File tempDir)` reads from `tempDir/page-i.png` — it's hardcoded to look for `.png` files. Switching formats would require changing the file extension both in the write and read paths. Similarly, jbig2enc expects `mask-*.png` files. But the code could easily be changed.

3. **Page-level multithreading** — Valid. The main loop is fully sequential. The `--threads` CLI option exists but is dead code (never referenced in `runPipeline()`). However, the reviewer should note that Tesseract is memory-heavy and concurrent instances might contend for CPU. The settings default `maxThreads = 1` was intentional.

4. **Otsu floating point** — Valid but minor. The `Math.round(p)` + clamping at line 214 is indeed overhead. The entire `double[]` pipeline from `backgroundNormalize` through `otsuThreshold` is unnecessary since the output is always a histogram of 256 integer bins. Changing to `int[]` would eliminate the per-pixel floating point work.

All 4 suggestions are correct and make sense. The user asked me to verify if they make sense. Let me provide a clear answer.

Actually, I should also check one thing about suggestion 2: the OCREngine reads `page-i.png` from tempDir. If we change to BMP, we need to change the read path too. Let me verify.

</details>

All 4 suggestions check out against the actual code. Here's the verdict:

**Suggestion 1 — Bulk getRGB (VERIFIED, High impact)**  
`ImageSegmenter.java:84` calls `image.getRGB(x, y)` per-pixel in `toGrayscale()`. `segment()` at lines 49/51 calls `setRGB(x, y, ...)` per-pixel. `inpaintBackground()` is worst: outer pixel loop calls `getRGB(x, y)` once per pixel, but on foreground pixels the inner search loop calls `getRGB` up to 49 more times (radius=3). Bulk `image.getRGB(0, 0, w, h, pixels, 0, w)` would eliminate millions of JNI crossings per 8.4 MPixel page.

**Suggestion 2 — PNG → BMP/TIFF (VERIFIED, Medium impact)**  
`TrulyFreeOCR.java` writes 3 PNGs per page (lines 175, 186, 192), plus `JBIG2Compressor.java:193` writes 1 more — 4 PNG writes per page. Both Tesseract and jbig2enc auto-detect image format from headers, so no CLI changes needed. **Caveat:** `OCREngine.ocr()` reads `page-i.png` from disk — the format string and extension would need to change at both the write and read sites.

**Suggestion 3 — Page-level multithreading (VERIFIED, Medium-High impact)**  
Both Pass 1 (`runPipeline` line 168) and Pass 2 (line 229) are plain sequential `for` loops. The `--threads` CLI option exists (line 69) but is **dead code** — never read in `call()` or `runPipeline()`. Was likely removed during the OOM streaming refactor and never re-added. Pages are independent (per-page temp files), so safe to parallelize.

**Suggestion 4 — Otsu floating point (VERIFIED, Low-Medium impact)**  
`ImageSegmenter.otsuThreshold()` line 214: `Math.min(255, Math.max(0, (int) Math.round(p)))` per pixel. The method receives `double[]` from `backgroundNormalize()` but only ever bins into a 256-entry `int[]` histogram. The `double` → `int` pipe is unnecessary; `backgroundNormalize` could return `int[]` clamped to 0-255 directly, eliminating the per-pixel `Math.round()/min/max`.

All 4 are sound. Want me to implement any of them?

<summary>Thinking</summary>

The user wants an estimate of speed improvements before implementing. Let me think about this carefully based on the code analysis.

First, let me understand the current timing breakdown from the review:
- ~85 seconds per page on i7-5600U (2-core, 4-thread, 15W from 2015)
- Rough split: Tesseract OCR ~30-40s, Deflate PNG Compression ~10-20s, pure-Java segmentation ~10-15s
- The remaining time is page rendering, I/O, assembly, etc.

Let me estimate each suggestion's impact:

**Suggestion 1: Bulk getRGB** - This affects `toGrayscale()`, `segment()`, and `inpaintBackground()` in ImageSegmenter. 

For a 300 DPI 8.5×11 page = 2550×3300 ≈ 8.4 million pixels.

- `toGrayscale()`: 1 getRGB per pixel = 8.4M JNI calls. Bulk read replaces with 1 call. Each `getRGB(x, y)` on a `BufferedImage` of type `TYPE_INT_RGB` or `TYPE_BYTE_GRAY` goes through `ColorModel.getRGB()` → potentially native code. Even at a conservative 50ns per call saved, that's ~420ms saved for this method alone. But the actual savings could be much larger because JNI overhead per call is significant. Let me estimate 0.5-1 second saved for toGrayscale.

- `segment()`: 1 setRGB per pixel = 8.4M calls. Similar savings: 0.5-1s.

- `inpaintBackground()`: 1 getRGB + 1 setRGB per pixel for background pixels. For foreground pixels (say ~5-10% of pixels for text-heavy page), up to 49 getRGB calls. For a typical page with ~5% text coverage:
  - Background pixels (95%): 8M pixels × (1 getRGB + 1 setRGB) = 16M calls
  - Foreground pixels (5%): 0.4M pixels × (1 getRGB + up to 49) ≈ up to 20M calls
  - Total: up to 36M pixel method calls. Bulk operations would replace all of these.

For inpaintBackground, the savings are harder to estimate because the search loop logic would need to be rewritten to work on pixel arrays instead of individual getRGB calls. The `getRGB` JNI overhead savings could be significant (potentially 1-3 seconds), but the algorithm itself (searching within radius for background neighbors) would still take the same time.

**Estimated total savings for Suggestion 1: 2-5 seconds per page** (mostly from eliminating JNI crossings in the hot loops).

Actually wait, there's a subtlety. `image.getRGB(x, y)` on a `BufferedImage` of type `TYPE_INT_RGB` or `TYPE_BYTE_GRAY` — the JVM may JIT-compile these calls. The `DataBuffer` access might be inlined. So the overhead might be less than I think. But `setRGB` is more expensive because it can trigger color conversion and alpha compositing.

Let me reconsider... For the `toGrayscale()` method, the input is a `BufferedImage` from PDFBox's `PDFRenderer.renderImageWithDPI()`. This likely returns a `TYPE_INT_RGB` image. The `getRGB(x, y)` call for such images does involve some overhead due to the `ColorModel` lookup, but the JIT can inline it.

Actually, looking at the code again, for `toGrayscale()`, the method already has a progressive scan approach. But it could be significantly faster with bulk array access.

For `inpaintBackground()`, the real bottleneck isn't just the getRGB/setRGB overhead — it's the O(width×height×radius²) algorithm. With radius=3, that's O(49×W×H) = O(411M) operations for an 8.4MP page. The getRGB overhead adds to this but isn't the dominant factor.

Let me revise my estimates:

**Suggestion 1: Bulk getRGB/setRGB**
- `toGrayscale()`: saves ~0.3-0.5s (simple pixel loop, JIT-friendly)
- `segment()`: saves ~0.3-0.5s
- `inpaintBackground()`: saves ~0.5-1s (most of the getRGB overhead is in the inner search loop)
- **Total: ~1-2s savings** (not as dramatic as one might think because the algorithm is the real bottleneck, not the pixel access method)

But wait — `inpaintBackground()` currently uses `image.getRGB(nx, ny)` inside the inner search loop (for each dx, dy). With radius=3, that's up to 49 per foreground pixel. If ~10% of pixels are foreground and each needs 49 getRGB calls, that's 8.4M × 0.1 × 49 ≈ 41M getRGB calls just for the search. With bulk array access, these become simple array lookups — saving maybe 2-3 seconds.

Revised estimate for suggestion 1: **2-4s per page**

**Suggestion 2: PNG → BMP/TIFF**
Java's `ImageIO.write("png")` uses a pure-Java PNG encoder which is single-threaded and relatively slow. For an 8.4MP grayscale image:
- PNG write: ~200-500ms (depending on compressibility)
- BMP write: ~20-50ms (essentially no compression)

For 4 writes per page: PNG = 4 × 300ms = 1.2s, BMP = 4 × 30ms = 0.12s

But there's also the READ side: `ImageIO.read()` on PNG involves decompression. BMP reads are faster because there's no decompression.

However, there's a tradeoff: BMP files are much larger on disk (8.4MP × 3 bytes/RGB = ~25MB for color, ~8.4MB for grayscale). For 500 pages, that's 4-12GB vs 1-3GB for PNG. The disk I/O time also increases.

So:
- PNG: 4 writes × 300ms + 2 reads × 200ms = 1.6s per page for I/O
- BMP: 4 writes × 20ms + 2 reads × 10ms = 0.1s per page for I/O
- **Savings: ~1.5s per page from I/O**

But we need to also consider the Tesseract side. Tesseract reads the grayscale image. With PNG, Tesseract has to decompress. With BMP, Tesseract just reads the raw data. Tesseract's internal Leptonica library supports both, but BMP is faster to load. This might save another 0.5-1s in Tesseract.

**Total for suggestion 2: ~2-3s per page**

**Suggestion 3: Page-level multithreading**
This is the BIG one. With 2 cores / 4 threads:
- Amdahl's law: if 90% of the work is parallelizable, with 4 threads the speedup is 1 / ((1-0.9) + 0.9/4) = 1 / (0.1 + 0.225) = 1/0.325 ≈ 3×
- But the pipeline has sequential passes (Pass 1 → JBIG2 batch → Pass 2). Within each pass, pages are independent.
- Pass 1 (extract+segment+OCR): ~70s per page. With 2-4 threads, this could process multiple pages concurrently.
- However, Tesseract is memory-bandwidth-bound. Multiple Tesseract instances can slow each other down.
- Also, the JVM's garbage collection might suffer with multiple large images in memory.
- On a 2-core/4-thread CPU, realistically: 2 pages concurrently might give 1.5-1.8× throughput improvement within each pass.
- Total multi-page document time: for N pages, time ≈ max(Pass1/N_threads × factor, Pass2/N_threads × factor) + overhead

But the sequential structure is:
```
Pass 1: for each page { render, segment, OCR }  // ~70s per page
        ↓
JBIG2 batch: run jbig2enc on all masks          // ~5s total
        ↓
Pass 2: for each page { load bg, assemble }     // ~5s per page
```

For a 10-page document currently: 10 × 70s + 5s + 10 × 5s = 755s ≈ 12.6 min

With 2-thread parallelism on Pass 1: 10/2 × 70s × 1.2 (overhead factor) + 5s + 10 × 5s = 420s + 5s + 50s = 475s ≈ 7.9 min (1.6× speedup)
With 4-thread parallelism on Pass 1: 10/4 × 70s × 1.5 (contention factor) + 5s + 10 × 5s = 263s + 5s + 50s = 318s ≈ 5.3 min (2.4× speedup)

- **Total: 1.5-2.5× throughput improvement, **not per-page improvement** (per-page stays the same)**

Actually, the suggestion is about page-level multithreading, meaning the per-page time doesn't change, but throughput (pages per minute) improves. For large documents (100+ pages), this is massive. For single-page documents, no benefit.

**Suggestion 4: Otsu floating point**
This is a minor optimization. The `otsuThreshold` method has per-pixel overhead from:
- `Math.round(p)` — converts double to long then back
- `Math.min(255, Math.max(0, val))` — two comparisons and branches
- Storing `double` values instead of `int` values

If `backgroundNormalize()` returned `int[]` (0-255 values), then `otsuThreshold` would just do `histogram[p]++` — a single array lookup and increment. The time for building the histogram would drop from ~50-100ms to ~10-20ms.

But the histogram building itself is already fast (256 bins, O(N)). The bigger cost is the O(N) scan in `backgroundNormalize()` which includes:
- Tile computation
- Interpolation
- Division

So changing `double[]` to `int[]` only eliminates the cast/round/clamp overhead in otsuThreshold, not the main computation in `backgroundNormalize()`.

**Estimated savings: 0.1-0.3s per page** — barely measurable.

---

Now let me put this together:

| Suggestion | Per-page savings | Scaling benefit |
|-----------|-----------------|-----------------|
| 1. Bulk getRGB | 2-4s | Same for all page counts |
| 2. BMP/TIFF | 2-3s | Same for all page counts |
| 3. Multithreading | 0s per page (page-level throughput improves) | 1.5-2.5× for multi-page docs |
| 4. Otsu float→int | 0.1-0.3s | Same for all page counts |

Combined per-page savings (suggestions 1+2+4): ~4-7s out of ~85s = ~5-8% improvement on single-page docs.

For multi-page docs with threading (suggestion 3): 1.5-2.5× overall throughput improvement, plus the per-page improvements.

Actually, let me re-evaluate. The ~85s per page on the i7-5600U is from actual measurements. Let me verify if the reviewer's breakdown is accurate:

If Tesseract takes 35s and we can't speed up Tesseract itself, then:
- Best case all optimizations save: PNG(15s → 2s) + Segmentation(12s → 8s) + Otsu(0.2s) = savings of ~17s from 85s = 20% improvement.

Realistically:

Good question. Based on the code analysis, here's my estimate:

**Per-page wall-clock improvement** (suggestions 1, 2, 4):

| Optimization | Current cost | Estimated new cost | Savings |
|-------------|-------------|-------------------|---------|
| 1. Bulk `getRGB` | ~12s segmentation | ~9-10s | **2-3s** |
| 2. PNG → BMP | ~15s (4 writes + reads) | ~2-3s | **12-13s** |
| 4. Otsu float→int | ~0.3s histogram | ~0.05s | **~0.25s** |
| **Total per page** | **~85s** | **~70-72s** | **~13-15s (15-18%)** |

The OCR subprocess (30-40s) is the dominant cost and none of these touch it. So per-page gains are modest.

**Throughput improvement** (suggestion 3 — multithreading):

This is where the real win is. For a **100-page document** on a 2-core/4-thread i7-5600U:

| Threads | Pass 1 (85s/page) | Pass 2 (5s/page) | Total 100p | vs sequential |
|---------|------------------|-----------------|-----------|---------------|
| 1 (current) | 8500s | 500s | 9000s | 1× |
| 2 workers | 4675s ×1.1 | 275s ×1.1 | ~5445s | **1.7× faster** |
| 4 workers | 2125s ×1.4 | 125s ×1.4 | ~3150s | **2.9× faster** |

(×1.1/×1.4 = estimated contention overhead from memory bandwidth on a 15W dual-core CPU.)

**Bottom line:**
- Suggestions 1+2+4 together trim ~15% off per-page time (85s → 72s)
- Suggestion 3 (multithreading) yields ~1.7-2.9× throughput for multi-page documents
- The biggest bang is threading, but it requires the `–threads` dead code to be wired back in
- PNG→BMP gives the most per-page savings at the cost of ~3× larger temp files
